Economic Supplement

The Crisis of China's Cotton Yarn Industry 228

— Wei Qi

The cotton yarn industry is one of China's largest industries today, with capital of about 130 million yuan and employing over 100,000 workers. The number of large and small merchants who rely on trading cotton, cotton yarn, and cotton cloth for a living is even greater. Moreover, cotton yarn is the raw material for cotton textiles, and cotton textiles are an indispensable necessity for the daily lives of the vast majority of Chinese people. This can be seen from the fact that cotton goods and cotton yarn account for the largest proportion of China's annual imports. Not only that, but the cotton yarn consolidated tax is also one of the government's most important sources of revenue, amounting to more than 20 million yuan annually. Therefore, the rise and fall of the cotton yarn industry is closely related to the national economy and the people's livelihood, which goes without saying. However, in recent years, Chinese-owned yarn mills have been affected externally by the world economic panic and the dumping of foreign yarn and cloth by imperialists, and internally by the competition and oppression of foreign-owned yarn mills in China, as well as by successive years of natural and man-made disasters. This has led to the collapse of the rural economy, a sharp decline in purchasing power, a market slump, and stagnant sales, plunging yarn mills across the country into a critical situation where they cannot continue to operate. All of these things have now become obvious facts, not theoretical issues.

Regarding the causes of the crisis in China's cotton yarn industry, according to my personal observations, there are roughly the following points:

(1) Insufficient Raw Cotton. Everyone knows that cotton is the raw material for cotton yarn, and cotton cloth is the product made from it. Therefore, the rise and fall of the cotton yarn industry is constantly determined by the high or low price of cotton and yarn. If cotton is cheap and yarn is expensive, then there is profit and prosperity; if cotton is expensive and yarn is cheap, then there is loss and decline. In the past, cotton in China was extremely cheap, not only sufficient for use, but also a major export product. However, since 1919, on the one hand, the number of domestic yarn mills has increased daily, and on the other hand, the increase in planting area and harvest amount has been minimal, so that domestic cotton is insufficient to meet the needs of various yarn mills, and a large amount of expensive foreign cotton has to be imported every year. Originally, the insufficiency of domestic raw cotton and the use of foreign raw cotton are not entirely related to the rise and fall of the yarn industry. Japan is one example. However, China's industry is backward, its technology is immature, and its capital is weak. Everything is behind others, and it cannot be compared with Japan after all. What it relies on is only cheap labor and low-priced raw materials. Now that raw cotton is insufficient and expensive foreign raw materials are used, it immediately becomes a problem. Moreover, in recent years, the high price of gold and the low price of silver, import tariffs, etc., have further increased the cost of finished products. Not only that, but the import of foreign cotton can also directly damage China's rural economy, leading to a reduction in farmers' purchasing power and affecting the sales of cotton yarn and cotton cloth. Therefore, insufficient raw cotton is one of the most fundamental causes of the crisis in China's cotton yarn industry. The following table lists the supply and consumption of cotton in China in the past ten years for reference. (Planting area is in mu, other units are in dan)

Year Planting Area Domestic Cotton Production Foreign Cotton Imports Total Supply Yarn Mill Consumption

1923 29,554,053 8,310,355 639,797 8,950,152 6,033,000

1924 29,771,577 7,144,642 161,862 7,306,504 5,891,000

1925 28,121,027 7,808,882 1,006,618 8,815,500 6,037,000

1926 27,349,727 7,534,351 1,866,505 9,400,856 6,581,000

1927 27,610,276 6,243,585 968,532 7,212,117 7,200,000

1928 31,926,311 6,722,108 804,582 7,526,690 7,566,600

1929 33,811,255 7,748,366 1,571,000 9,319,366 7,338,000

1930 37,593,012 8,809,567 2,630,949 11,440,516 8,939,280

1931 37,593,012 6,399,780 3,862,864 10,662,644 8,859,968

1932 31,637,779 8,637,637 3,049,592 11,155,229 8,965,935

(2) Inferior Quality of Chinese Cotton. Not only is the output of cotton in China insufficient to meet demand, but its quality is also very poor, making it unsuitable for spinning fine yarn and double-strand thread. This is also very clear from the table above, that is, the amount of cotton consumed by Chinese yarn mills has not increased dramatically, and the output of domestic cotton has not declined sharply; but the amount of foreign cotton imported by customs has increased rapidly, especially American cotton and Egyptian cotton. This is because American cotton and Egyptian cotton are all fine-staple cotton. In recent years, it has been difficult for China to import good American varieties in large quantities, but because cotton farmers lack knowledge and do not know how to select seeds and retain good ones, the original long-fiber American varieties have gradually degraded after several years and become coarse. According to the results of the investigation, the output of this long-fiber cotton was 2,079,543 dan in 1929, 3,169,889 dan in 1930, 2,523,650 dan in 1931, and 3,065,995 dan in 1932. On average, it is still less than 3 million dan per year, and of these 3 million dan, due to the adulteration of coarse cotton by cotton merchants, the actual amount that can be used for fine yarn is probably only half, that is, 1.5 million dan. Compared with the current amount of fine yarn produced domestically, the difference is actually far. As a result, most yarn mills have to use American cotton and Egyptian cotton to make up for the shortage. The following table lists the ratio of various types of cotton sold and used by domestic yarn mills in the past four years:

Year Chinese Cotton American Cotton Indian Cotton Egyptian Cotton Other

1929 68.25 13.66 17.99 0.04 0.00

1930 63.11 13.60 22.76 0.21 0.30

1931 49.67 26.43 23.29 0.43 0.18

1932 52.13 38.58 8.81 0.45 0.03

(3) Oppression by the Dumping of Foreign Yarn and Cloth. In the past, China was bound by the agreed tariff, so it could not freely increase tariffs to protect its domestic industry. Although the tariff autonomy has now been recovered, it is still far from protection in practice. Generally speaking, China's tariffs are still very low compared to other countries; and in recent years, all capitalist countries in the world have been hit by an unprecedented economic panic, with production piling up like mountains. If they want to invest in foreign countries, they are blocked by tariff barriers; so they have no choice but to dump large quantities in China, which has a relatively backward industry and relatively low tariffs. Just look at the year-by-year increase in foreign goods imported into China, and you will know. The following are the figures for cotton textiles and cotton yarn since 1921 to prove this. (Unit: customs taels)

Year Cotton Textiles Cotton Yarn

1921 145,701,479 72,158,170

1922 154,124,026 71,229,571

1923 132,871,137 44,178,897

1924 154,471,049 36,867,638

1925 152,015,520 41,353,981

1926 172,122,233 31,163,048

1932 72,574,258 9,357,973

Note: It should be specially noted in the above table that the gradual decrease in the cotton yarn section since 1922 is due to the dumping by foreign merchants setting up factories in China.

(4) Oppression by the Dumping of Foreign-Owned Yarn Mills in China. China's cotton yarn industry is not only oppressed by the dumping of foreign cotton yarn and cloth, but also by the dumping of foreign-owned yarn mills in China. Because China is bound by unequal treaties, imperialists can freely set up factories in China. There are roughly the following benefits for imperialists to set up factories in China: First, using extremely cheap labor; Second, using low-priced raw materials in China; Third, products sold in China are exempt from tariffs and transportation costs. At present, the factories set up by imperialists in China are mainly yarn mills, and Japan is the first among them, followed by the United Kingdom. According to a survey by the Ministry of Industry, there are a total of 43 Japanese-owned yarn mills in China, with a capital of 1,078,000,000 yuan and 1,582,056 spindles. According to another survey, there are 4 British-owned yarn mills in China, with a capital of 20,000,000 yuan and 205,320 spindles. From this point of view, only Japan plays a major role in the Chinese cotton yarn market. Japanese imperialists have always pursued a consistent policy of dumping and invading China. After the two incidents of September 18th and January 28th, although they were slightly hit by the severe boycott of the Chinese people, in order to break through this difficulty, they further devalued and dumped their products to break the Chinese anti-smuggling line and regain the Chinese market. But what is the annual output of the yarn mills they set up in China? Just look at the table below and you will know.

Cotton Yarn Cotton Cloth

Year Chinese Yarn Mill Output Japanese Yarn Mill Output British Yarn Mill Output Chinese Yarn Mill Output Japanese Yarn Mill Output British Yarn Mill Output

1923 1,019,718 422,250 31,800 | | | | | |

1924 1,171,575 543,718 84,500 2,490,475 1,260,000 | | |

1927 1,261,548 717,769 105,522 4,259,666 4,739,704 | | |

Note: The figures from 1923 to 1930 are based on a survey by the Chinese Yarn Mill Association. Cotton yarn is in bales, and cotton cloth is in pieces. The figures for 1931 and 1932 are based on a survey by the Bank of China. Cotton yarn is in bales, and cotton cloth is in pieces.

(5) Weak Capital. There are a total of 82 Chinese-owned yarn mills nationwide, with 2,522,300 spindles; although there are 39 more mills and 940,244 more spindles than Japanese-owned yarn mills in China, the capital is not increasing in direct proportion, but decreasing in inverse proportion, that is, Chinese-owned yarn mills have a total capital of only 130,000,000 yuan. Japanese-owned yarn mills in China account for more than 680 yuan per spindle, while Chinese-owned yarn mills account for only more than 50 yuan per spindle. Therefore, Chinese-owned yarn mills often have businesses larger than their capital, resulting in extremely difficult financial turnover. If they encounter competition from foreign goods and foreign merchants, stagnant sales, and inability to borrow money, they will immediately go bankrupt and declare bankruptcy.

(6) Immature Technology. Chinese-owned yarn mills are not only weak in capital, but also immature in technology. For example, Japanese-owned yarn mills in China use only 240 workers per 10,000 spindles to spin 20-count yarn, while Chinese-owned yarn mills must use 350 to 750 workers per 10,000 spindles to spin the same 20-count yarn. Therefore, although Chinese-owned yarn mills have more spindles and employ more workers than Japanese-owned yarn mills in China, the output increases very little, resulting in very high costs. Not only that, but most of the goods produced are uneven and of inferior quality.

(7) Financial Capital Does Not Cooperate. As mentioned above, Chinese yarn mills are weak in capital, but if financial capital is their backing and cooperates with them, it will not be difficult to barely support them and overcome the current difficulties. However, China's financial capital has never attached much importance to industrial investment, and is only enthusiastic about government bonds and real estate. Although a part of financial capital is also used by industry, due to the higher market interest rates and very harsh conditions, the interest rate is even one cent and four or five li per month. Therefore, such loans are not so much to rescue China's industry as to exploit and destroy China's industry. But what is the situation of Chinese financial capital lending to yarn mills? According to the recent two-year business reports of Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank and Bank of China, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank lent more than 23 million yuan to industry in 1931, accounting for 34.30% of the total loans. Among them, the textile industry accounted for 42.78% of the industrial loans. In 1932, the total amount of loans to the textile industry was more than 14 million taels, an increase of about 42% compared to 1931. In 1931, Bank of China lent a total of 33,674,925 yuan to industry, accounting for 10.14% of the total loans. Among them, yarn mills accounted for 47.9% of the industrial loans. In 1932, the total amount of loans to industry was 38,435,423 yuan, an increase of 7,237,769 yuan compared to 1931, accounting for 11.46% of the total loans. Among them, yarn mills accounted for 61.9% of the industrial loans. The Bank of China is very satisfied with these figures, saying that "it has done its best to maintain industry." But in reality, due to the high interest rates and the reluctance of other financial capital to lend to yarn mills, it is still of little benefit to the yarn mills themselves.

(8) Collapse of the Rural Economy and Sharp Decline in Farmers' Purchasing Power. Although cotton yarn and cotton cloth are necessities for the daily lives of farmers, due to the invasion of imperialism over the years, the destruction and exploitation by large and small warlords, and the destruction and attacks by natural disasters and bandits, the rural areas are becoming increasingly collapsed, farmers' purchasing power is declining sharply, and the sales of cotton yarn are stagnant. Because China's cotton yarn is not like raw silk, which is mainly based on the foreign market and supplemented by the domestic market, quite the opposite, China's cotton yarn almost relies on the domestic market; therefore, the collapse of the rural economy and the reduction of farmers' purchasing power have become a fatal blow to China's cotton yarn industry.

(9) Shrinking Sales Market. The so-called shrinking sales market refers to the loss of the four northeastern provinces. Since the September 18th Incident, after Japanese imperialists forcibly occupied the four northeastern provinces by force, not only did they lose vast land and abundant resources, but also because of the arrival of the iron hooves of Japanese imperialists in trade, they almost completely monopolized it. Moreover, after the establishment of the so-called Manchuria, they freely set up customs to stipulate tax rates and heavily levy commodity taxes on goods imported from mainland China. As a result, the vast market in the Northeast, which used to absorb light industrial products from mainland China, has seen a sharp decline in goods shipped in recently. Let's not talk about other things for the time being, let's just talk about cotton goods! Cotton textiles decreased from 11.6 million taels in 1931 after the incident to 8.3 million taels in the previous year; cotton yarn decreased from 20 million taels to 4.9 million taels, and it will undoubtedly decrease even more last year and this year. Therefore, the loss of the Northeast market is one of the main reasons for the current crisis in China's cotton yarn industry.

(10) Inadequate National Protection. It has become a consensus that the development of a country's industry depends on the strong protection and assistance of the country, especially for countries with backward industries. It goes without saying for the past of our government, and it is still not detached from protection even now. For example, foreign-owned yarn mills in China can purchase cotton and sell yarn, and can pass through the country after paying one tax, while Chinese-owned yarn mills cannot do so. There are still many exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes in various inland provinces. Another example is the cotton yarn consolidated tax regulations implemented in February 1931. Due to treaty relations, they cannot be exclusively beneficial to Chinese-owned yarn mills, but are treated equally; but in reality, they are still beneficial to foreign-owned yarn mills in China. In addition, there are many, many more, which are really too numerous to mention, but from this, we can get a glimpse of the government's inadequate protection of the cotton yarn industry.

In addition to this, such as the obsolescence of machinery, the irrationality of production and sales, and the shortsightedness of the yarn mill authorities who do not know how to unite, all are sufficient to constitute a crisis; but due to the limited space, I will not go into details.

The Relationship Between Cotton Grading and the Textile Industry 229

— Di Jian'an

The primary purpose of cotton grading is to facilitate the use of cotton by the textile industry and minimize unnecessary losses. Although England is not a cotton-producing country, it advocates for cotton quality standards. Textile companies rely on these standards to purchase raw cotton that meets their needs. Consequently, its textile industry is the most developed in the world. Our country is known as the world's third-largest cotton producer, yet cotton grading is still lacking. Thus, even good cotton lacks proper protection, often leading to its obscurity. Inferior cotton, on the other hand, is everywhere, which significantly hinders the development of our country's textile industry. In recent years, textile factories have favored foreign cotton due to its superior quality and ease of purchase, increasingly abandoning domestic cotton. This has led to a surge in foreign cotton imports and a decline in domestic cotton prices, causing rural bankruptcies and sluggish yarn sales, ultimately harming textile businesses, cotton merchants, and cotton farmers alike. To remedy this situation, it is imperative to promote cotton grading; however, promoting cotton grading requires the concerted effort of the entire textile industry. Due to the lack of detailed regulations for cotton grading in our country, each textile factory prioritizes its own interests. When purchasing raw cotton, penalties are imposed for poor quality, but no rewards are given for good quality, resulting in short-term gains at the expense of long-term harm. The fact that yarn factories do not follow cotton grading methods not only endangers the yarn factories themselves, but also causes significant damage to cotton-producing areas. For example, before the tenth year of the Republic of China (1921), northern Taicang produced black seed cotton. Cotton farmers were diligent in selecting cotton, resulting in clean, white, and high-quality cotton suitable for spinning around 20 counts. It was highly appreciated by yarn factories in Wuxi and Shanghai, which set up cotton purchasing offices in Taicang. Unfortunately, the buyers did not reward quality and penalize inferiority, often manipulating cotton farmers. Honest farmers with good cotton could not obtain high prices, while cunning farmers could sell inferior cotton at a reasonable price. The buyers manipulated the market, monopolizing and exploiting it. Farmers became unwilling to diligently select cotton and instead followed suit. Within a few years, good cotton gradually disappeared, and the quality declined daily, with yarn counts becoming coarser. The factories suffered significantly, with some declaring bankruptcy or closing their purchasing offices. The cotton production of Taicang was devastated, and it will not be easy to restore its former glory. Furthermore, the bankruptcy of the Yu Zhong Yarn Factory in Anqing the year before last was largely due to unfair inspection of raw cotton purchases. Cunning cotton merchants bribed inspectors, leading to the unlimited purchase of extremely inferior cotton. This angered some impartial individuals who directly transported the purchased cotton to Shanghai and other places for sale, unwilling to sell it to Yu Zhong. Because the factory used inferior cotton to spin yarn, the yarn quality was poor, and sales were sluggish. In some cases, the cotton could not even be spun. When the factory wanted to purchase better cotton, it was no longer available locally and had to be purchased from Shanghai, which increased costs and led to the risk of bankruptcy. Examples like these are numerous. Therefore, the decline of the textile industry in recent years, which has impacted the collapse of the national economy, stems primarily from the fact that textile factories do not know how to grade raw cotton. When purchasing cotton, they only consider the cotton price; they do not carefully assess the quality. Good cotton prices are not easily increased, while inferior cotton enjoys undeserved benefits. Cotton merchants, brokers, and farmers do not focus on improving cotton production but instead resort to deception. The textile industry bemoans the poor quality of domestic cotton, but it does not realize that the poor quality of domestic cotton is due to the factories' improper use of personnel and unfair selection, which contributes to the problem. People should blame the factories for their own misdeeds, which have added to our country's woes, instead of blaming others. How unclear this is! The reasons for this are as follows:

(1) Lack of Communication and Standardized Rules in the Textile Industry: Each factory's inspectors rely solely on their own experience to identify cotton quality, without any communication! There is no exchange of individual experiences or establishment of unified standards, which results in inspectors having different levels of ability, creating opportunities for cotton merchants to exploit and engage in fraud.

(2) Constraints of Low Yarn Prices: When yarn prices are low and do not match raw cotton prices, buyers cater to the owners' preferences and cannot purchase good cotton at high prices. They only care about the cost-effectiveness of cotton grades, resulting in the purchase of inferior goods. This seems cheap but is actually costly, affecting yarn quality and increasing waste cotton. In the end, the losses are greater than if they had purchased good cotton.

(3) Price Gouging by Buyers: The buyers or purchasing offices dispatched by textile factories are subject to the factory's price limits. Therefore, they suppress superior quality and assist inferior quality in order to balance their price gouging, regardless of the future of cotton production in that area. For example, if the average market price of cotton is 40 yuan, and the cotton is of superior quality, the price should be increased by 3 yuan, but the buyer only adds 2 yuan. Conversely, if the cotton is of inferior quality, the price should be reduced by 3 yuan, but the buyer only reduces it by 2 yuan in order to balance the price. This leaves the cotton farmer without any guarantees, and the cotton gradually deteriorates.

(4) Unreasonable Handling of Forward Cotton: Textile factories and cotton merchants often have forward contracts. Once the price is set, if the market price of cotton is lower than the agreed price at the time of delivery, the factory will often find various faults, such as returning the goods, increasing the weight, or deducting moisture, to compensate for their losses. Conversely, cotton merchants may also breach the contract by delivering inferior cotton, leading to frequent disputes. However, if cotton merchants deliver good cotton, the factory cannot increase the price due to the agreed price, resulting in criticism of punishing the bad and not rewarding the good.

(5) Competition in Trade: Another reason why it is difficult to obtain higher prices for good cotton in the raw cotton market is competition among businesses. If one company offers a particularly high price for good cotton, other companies often misunderstand and think that the price is being inflated. In order to develop their stores, they indiscriminately raise prices regardless of whether the cotton is good or not. This causes market chaos, and everyone suffers losses. Therefore, cotton merchants feel helpless in promoting good cotton, which leads to a decrease in good cotton.

(6) Corrupt Practices: Textile factory inspectors often privately accept bribes from sellers or are influenced by personal relationships. Their inspections vary from person to person, without a fixed approach. This leads to manipulation and oppression. Honest cotton merchants with good cotton often sell their cotton below the average price because they are not good at maneuvering, while cunning cotton merchants fraudulently obtain high prices and boast of their abilities. This causes honest cotton merchants to dwindle, while everyone strives to be cunning. This greatly impacts the improvement of cotton quality in our country.

The above reasons are unavoidable facts for textile factories. Therefore, if our country's textile industry wants to eliminate these malpractices and develop its business, it must unanimously promote cotton grading.

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has long paid attention to cotton grading in our country. It has referenced the American cotton grade standards, collected cotton samples from various regions, and conducted research. It has made comprehensive plans for the national cotton production, and based on years of research, it has tentatively set standards. Under the same scientific theory, there is a distinction between types and grades, praising the superior and criticizing the inferior, so that cotton from various regions can have a corresponding value. This can facilitate cotton trading procedures, maintain commercial fairness, improve quality, and develop the future of the cotton industry. The categories of cotton are temporarily divided into six types based on differences in varieties and quality: long-staple American cotton, short-staple American cotton, black-seed Chinese cotton, white-seed Chinese cotton, coarse cotton, and extra-coarse cotton. As for grades, they are generally divided into five grades, with four half-grades: first grade is superior grade, second grade is high grade, third grade is medium grade, fourth grade is low grade, and fifth grade is inferior grade. The length of cotton fibers is subject to separate length standards. Observing our country's cotton market, the basic standard is medium-grade American cotton with a length of 7/8 inch (implicitly referring to the raw material for Zhengzhou cotton spinning 20s as the standard). The price of cotton from various regions is determined by adjusting the price based on this basic standard, considering the grade and length of the cotton fibers. For example, regardless of where American cotton is produced, if its grade and length are higher than the basic standard, it should receive a higher price. If its grade and length are lower than the basic standard, it should be appropriately discounted. Even cotton produced in the same region should have different prices based on the quality. (The bureau has a table of adjustments for the tentative cotton standards for reference.) This will greatly benefit the needs of the textile industry. Moreover, the grading conditions are based on the color of the cotton, the amount of impurities, and the quality of ginning. Therefore, high-grade cotton produces superior yarn with less waste cotton, while low-grade cotton produces inferior yarn with more waste cotton, which is closely related to textile production. The category of cotton and the length of the cotton fibers are related to the yarn count. If the textile industry adopts these standards and becomes familiar with the grading methods, all problems can be easily solved. If they want to spin a certain type of yarn, they can use the appropriate grade of cotton, making allocation convenient and minimizing unnecessary waste. When ordering futures, they can specify the type and grade of cotton and the price, forming a contract. If the cotton merchant delivers cotton that is of a higher grade than specified, the factory should increase the price accordingly. Conversely, the price should be reduced if the grade is lower. This type of transaction is fair. As for market price fluctuations, that is a separate issue. Neither the buyer nor the seller should engage in selfish behavior that disregards public reason due to losses. Furthermore, the government will eventually have regulations on cotton grades, and cotton merchants should establish a cotton grade inspection committee. This will stimulate the interest of cotton merchants and farmers in sorting cotton and provide a path for improvement. The work of adjusting and selecting cotton will gradually improve, and the quality of cotton will soon improve. Good cotton will be protected by grades and receive a high price, which will promote the development of the cotton planting industry. The "quality" and "quantity" issues of our country's cotton production can be resolved without further discussion. Recently, the National Economic Commission's Cotton Industry Control Committee also has plans to promote cotton grading, which is a prerequisite for the development of the cotton industry. The textile industry, being the highest level of the cotton industry, has such a close relationship with cotton grading. Why not cooperate with the government to achieve this goal?

Silver and Banking Industries Cautiously Conduct Business 232

| Number of New Accounts is Less Than One-Third of Previous Years |

In previous years, silver and banking industries would be in the process of expanding their business after the Lantern Festival, opening new current accounts and accounts, with at least 80% to 90% being opened. However, this year, due to poor performance last winter and the decline of commerce, many outstanding debts could not be repaid. Thus, everyone is being cautious and has not yet opened accounts as much as possible. According to people in the industry, the number of new accounts opened this year is less than one-third of previous years. (For example, if 600 accounts were opened in previous years, less than 200 accounts will be opened this year.) All the extracted accounts must be carefully considered before a decision is made. Therefore, this year, those outside the industry who want to rely on the financial community for financing may not get their wish.

Securities: Bond Market Hovered Last Week 233

Resulting in a Slight Increase of About Half a Yuan

First Half of the Week: Investor Confidence Remained Steady and Continued to Rise

Second Half of the Week: Atmosphere Became Murky and Market Softened

Last week, from February 26th to March 1st, the China Merchants Securities Exchange was closed for one day on Monday for the settlement of February futures. There were a total of five trading days. The April futures contract began trading on Tuesday and has resumed two trading sessions each in the morning and afternoon. Initially, investor confidence remained steady, silver was abundant, and short sellers covered their positions, leading to continued gains. Subsequently, as the situation between Japan and Russia became increasingly precarious and the puppet regime in the Northeast brazenly declared independence, the atmosphere became somewhat murky, and the market hovered and softened. However, this did not have a significant impact on the government bond market. In reality, market prices were already high, which easily triggered profit-taking and speculation. Even if the market does not fall back in the short term, it will still fluctuate. The market was closed for settlement on Monday. On Tuesday, the April futures contract began trading, and the full day of four trading sessions resumed. Short sellers covered their positions, and arbitrage trading was also quite active, with market prices rising uniformly by several jiao to about one yuan. The situation was roughly the same on Wednesday, with continued gains of four or five jiao to eight or nine jiao due to abundant silver and few sellers. On Thursday, news suddenly spread that the situation between Japan and Russia had deteriorated, and the puppet regime was inaugurated, which, although inevitable, inevitably caused investor sentiment to waver slightly. Profit-taking emerged, and market prices fell by about half a yuan. Although there was an impact, it was very minor. On Friday, retail investors took profits, and large investors continued to sell, with market prices remaining sluggish. The decline continued by five to seven jiao. On Saturday, although the decline was only about three or four jiao, and some even saw a slight gain of one or two jiao, the trend did not reverse throughout the day, indicating that buyers have become more cautious. As a result of the week, market prices saw a slight increase of about half a yuan compared to the previous week. The total transaction volume was 56,852,000 yuan. The highs, lows, gains, and losses are listed below for comparison. (Unit: yuan, Transaction Unit: 100 yuan)

On the Definition and Supplement to Medical Rights 238

— Wang Qizhang

The issues of medical ethics and morality in medicine have been much discussed in recent years. Those who know speak of it, those who understand debate it, but each person sees it differently. It is impossible for everyone to practice what they preach. This is a shame for the medical profession. However, new customs and teachings take time to develop. It has always been this way. If we can find someone like Zhuang Yue to mold and shape us, then in a hundred years, we might be transformed. My learned friend, Mr. Song Guobin, has repeatedly emphasized medical ethics and has even written a monumental work on physician ethics, which is truly a pioneering voice in the development of ethical standards in the medical field. It should not be regarded as just another ordinary opinion. Those in the know believe that his contribution is no less than that of Yu the Great. However, in this turbid world, everyone is vying for rights. Even gentlemen who clearly understand the difference between profit and righteousness cannot avoid the struggle for rights. Even those who seek tranquility and non-action still struggle to break free, let alone we doctors who are immersed in the hustle and bustle of the world, constantly involved in commercial transactions. This is why Liu Xiahui is so admirable. Recently, Mr. Song's proposition of "Five Rights for Physicians" is a continuation of his work on physician ethics, and it truly speaks to the heart. In fact, the essence of morality and ethics is not an obligation that corresponds to the rights of others. Rather, it is the responsibility, path, scope, and concept that everyone under the heavens should fulfill. It is not something that only begins to be practiced because of the rights of the object. Therefore, it differs from law. Although physician ethics is not the same as that of ordinary people, its guiding principles are fundamental and universally valid, and are rooted in ethical principles. It should not be restricted to the duties of physicians and misinterpreted as a price for rights. Here, I argue from a legal perspective. Because physicians are subject to legal constraints, they must fulfill their legal obligations. At the same time, they are also protected by law, and can thus acquire legal rights. This is a characteristic of the relative constraint and relative maintenance of rights and obligations that exists between them. Therefore, law implicitly embodies the means to remedy moral shortcomings, but it does not constitute morality itself. Those who discuss law have always believed that law is established to compensate for the inadequacies of morality. But in fact, even if morality is complete, there should still be law. To reiterate, morality is the necessary path in life, while law is valuable when it is in place but not needed. Therefore, the righteousness and benefit of morality are like tendencies towards the east and west, while the righteousness and benefit of law are the assertions of human desires. They cannot be equated. After reading Mr. Song's "Five Rights" theory, I deeply feel that it is not a discussion of morality, but rather one based on law. Therefore, I add several legal rights as a supplement. Mr. Song will surely agree with my words, won't he?

(1) The right to use narcotics: Such as opium, morphine, heroin, and other narcotics that are legally prohibited. For the general public, not only are they not allowed to use them, but they are also not allowed to sell them. However, physicians can arbitrarily prescribe them to people for internal use, which is equivalent to applying them. If a pharmacist dispenses and sells them to people, it is no different from selling them. So why do physicians have this exclusive right and are not prohibited? It is limited to treating illnesses and relieving pain in good faith.

(2) The right to use sharp instruments to cut the human body: According to criminal law, inflicting bodily harm on others with any instrument should be punished as assault. Physicians, however, hold knives and scissors, arbitrarily excising intestines, removing tumors, opening abdomens, and dissecting skulls, performing almost all the cruelest acts in the world without being prohibited. Why? It is limited to treating illnesses and relieving pain in good faith.

(3) The right to detain and infringe upon a person's freedom: Physicians have the right to prohibit patients from going out and moving freely. This is not only for the mentally ill, but also for ordinary patients, under appropriate and necessary conditions, their actions can be monitored and their freedom infringed upon. In the field of plastic surgery, the constraints are even more severe. Why are such imminent threats of violence not subject to sanctions? It is limited to treating illnesses and relieving pain in good faith.

(4) The right to perform abortions: According to criminal law, using drugs or other methods to induce abortion in pregnant women is a crime. However, physicians are allowed to perform such acts at any time without being prohibited. Why? It is limited to maintaining the safety of the mother's body in good faith, or because of the treatment of a disease.

(5) The right to perform indecent acts: "Indecent acts" include selling or displaying indecent and obscene documents and pictures, as well as exposing the genitals or performing illegal acts. Also, taking advantage of a person's loss of consciousness or inability to resist to commit indecent acts is subject to appropriate penalties. However, physicians have books on reproductive physiology and pathology, diagrams of intercourse and fertilization, and examinations of the vulva in obstetrics and gynecology. Furthermore, exploration may be necessary, and if examination is impossible or surgery is required, anesthesia may be administered, causing loss of consciousness and inability to resist, and then the procedure is forcibly performed. So why is this same indecent act not prohibited for physicians? It is limited to academic research and relieving pain in good faith.

There are also special rights such as harming corpses, and many others. If ordinary people were to do these things, they would be committing crimes and inviting disaster. Therefore, those who abide by the law and serve the public are constantly trembling with fear, anxious to avoid them. But we doctors do them with impunity. Is it because of the supreme authority and dignity of physicians? Now, let us examine ourselves and observe. If the powerful and wealthy are tyrannical, it will ruin the country. If doctors are tyrannical, they will harm people. The saying that "great thieves do not wield bows and spears" is most worthy of our warning and deep caution. I have written this article because I believe that Mr. Song's "Five Rights" theory is written for the physicians' personal rights. My supplementary "Five Rights" theory is based on the physicians' special rights that transcend criminal law. However, both are based on legal principles and not on ethical principles. So, is the hard work of physicians in public health and relieving human suffering the price for these previous five rights and the latter five rights? That is difficult to say. As for morality and ethics, although they are also human endeavors, there are often things that arise from human nature without human intervention. Birds know filial piety, lambs know gratitude. Even animals are like this, let alone humans. Therefore, I say that those who speak of ethics should not equate it with rights and obligations. I ask Mr. Song what he thinks.

Treatment and Prevention of Tetanus (Continued) 239

— Qu Shaoheng

(2) Local Therapy: The local wound should be opened as much as possible. After the pus, necrotic tissue, and foreign objects are completely removed, apply iodine, hydrogen peroxide, or "Balsamum Perurinum" to wash the wound. Then, fill it with 50-100 units of antitoxin. In addition, there is also the method of continuously dissolving the wound with 0.5-0.75% carbolic acid water and irradiating the wound with an artificial alpine sun lamp. However, although corrosive methods were appreciated in ancient times, they are now prohibited.

(3) Serum Therapy: The therapeutic effect of antitoxin serum varies depending on the method of injection.

There are six methods of injection: subcutaneous injection, intravenous injection, arterial injection, intraneural injection, intracerebral injection, and intrathecal injection. The choice should be determined by the physician's observation. However, when injecting into the brain or spinal cord, the same amount of cerebrospinal fluid as the serum to be injected should be withdrawn first. The dosage is 100-150 units per injection into the brain or spinal cord, 100-300 units per intravenous injection, and 100 units per intraneural injection.

(4) Drug Therapy: Hydrated Chloral Enema, five times a day, 1 cc each time. Pontopon or morphine subcutaneous injection, several times a day, 0.02 each time. Veronal Luminal subcutaneous injection, five times a day, 0.4 each time. Numal "Roche" internal, five times a day, one tablet each time (each tablet contains 0.06). 15% magnesium sulfate solution intravenous or intramuscular injection, two to three times a day, 10 cc each time. For severe cases, 10 cc of this solution can be injected into the lumbar spine. If muscle relaxation is not observed 30 minutes after the injection, lower the head. If respiratory paralysis occurs after the magnesium sulfate injection, wash the lumbar spine with physiological saline and inject 5% calcium chloride intravenously. For those with difficulty breathing, perform a tracheotomy and oxygen inhalation.

For neonatal tetanus, in addition to umbilical cord disinfection, hydrated chloral enema, two to three times a day, 0.25-0.5 each time. Chloroform inhalation. Bromine agent internal use. Within the first 24-28 hours, inject 50 units of tetanus antitoxin around the umbilical cord and 50 units under the spinal dura. 5 cc of 4% magnesium sulfate solution subcutaneous injection, twice on the first day, then once a day thereafter.

I have a niece who studied medicine with me from a young age. She married into the Xie family of Luhang and had a son named Zongxuan. He died at only seven months old. She was overwhelmed with grief, but thinking of her young son in her arms, she continued the family line as a consolation. She took good care of him and cherished him like a precious pearl. At the age of seven, he could understand poetry and prose. Everyone who saw him praised him, saying that the Xie family had an heir. One day in October of the 21st year of the Republic of China, he was playing in the courtyard in front of the door with a glass bottle in his hand. He accidentally fell and broke the bottle, injuring his hand. He was bleeding profusely. His mother immediately applied medicine and bandaged it. Seven days later, she came to my house for something. He was still playing with the other children during the day, but in the evening he had a slight fever. By midnight, his fever was high, and he suddenly showed signs of lockjaw. His mother immediately suspected tetanus. However, because she lived in the countryside and it was the middle of the night, there was no doctor to call and no medicine to use. She had no choice but to wait for dawn and send him to a hospital in Shanghai. When they examined the wound, it smelled unbearably rotten. Examination revealed tetanus bacteria. Serum was immediately injected, but it was ineffective. It is common for young children to fall and get injured. However, because the injury allowed tetanus bacteria to enter, it was fatal. Although it can be said to be fate, it was actually a mistake in the initial treatment. I was moved by this, so I wrote this article to warn the world.

Common Sense Question and Answer on Diseases 240

— Cheng Hanzhang

(2)(15) Croupous Pneumonia (Continued)

(Q) What are the different variations in the symptoms and course of croupous pneumonia?

(A) There are various variations, such as central pneumonia, migratory pneumonia, drunkard's pneumonia, asthenic pneumonia, pediatric pneumonia, and geriatric pneumonia.

(Q) What is central pneumonia?

(A) Central pneumonia has the same symptoms as the common type, but the lesion is limited to the hilar region and does not reach the edge.

(Q) What is migratory pneumonia?

(A) It means that the pneumonia lesion migrates from one lobe of the lung to another. Therefore, the symptoms continue to wax and wane, and the course of the disease is prolonged.

(Q) What is drunkard's pneumonia?

(A) Drunkard's pneumonia presents very severe symptoms during its course. They already complain of intense general fatigue in the early stages of the disease, fall into delirium, have tremors in their fingers, and see hallucinations of various small animals. They mostly take the path to death.

(Q) What is asthenic pneumonia?

(A) The patient is very weak, the lips and tongue are dry, the muscles tremble, and they fall into a coma. The course is very severe. There are various types of fever. The sputum often does not have a rusty color, and there is also a lack of sputum. There are also symptoms such as typhoid fever, with splenomegaly, proteinuria, and flatulence. Jaundice is also present.

(Q) What is pediatric pneumonia like?

(A) It does not start with chills, but often has severe delirium and convulsions, and very little sputum. The prognosis is generally good.

(Q) What is geriatric pneumonia like?

Page 18

(A) The onset is very gradual: there is less fever, but the heart is easily weakened, and the danger is great.

(Q) When does croupous pneumonia not present typical symptoms?

(A) It does not present typical symptoms when the patient has heart disease, emphysema, kidney disease, or excessive fat. If a person already has a wasting disease, there is a risk of early heart failure.

(Q) Are there any complications during the course of this disease?

(A) Yes, such as dry pleurisy, empyema, pulmonary gangrene, and liver abscess. There are also complications of pericarditis or meningitis.

(Q) What is the prognosis of croupous pneumonia?

(A) Generally, there is not much danger in young people. The prognosis is poor for the elderly, patients with heart disease, emphysema, kyphosis, diabetes, myopathy, kidney disease, pregnancy, and drunkards.

(Q) How should this disease be treated?

(A) The patient should be absolutely bedridden and quiet. Apply warm, moist compresses to the chest. Place ice packs on the heart and head. Give liquid foods. Internally, administer ipecac infusion, senega infusion, and asafoetida water as expectorants. Inject camphor, digitalis, and caffeine as cardiac stimulants. Quinine injections or internal administration of Optochin can be used as antipyretics. Pneumonia serum can be injected in children. (End)

More on Gonococci 241

— Zhu Yanggao

Since Neisser discovered gonococci in 1879, Bumm later definitively recognized it as the causative agent of gonorrhea. This is because he purely cultured this coccus using artificial methods (pure culture means culturing one specific bacteria from a mixture of bacteria), and was able to use this cultured gonococcus to create an artificial (intentional) true gonorrhea in the urethra of a healthy person. Thus, the previous doubts about the causative agent were completely dispelled.

The nature of gonococcus itself can be said to have been thoroughly researched to this day. We can even divide gonococcus into several subtypes (this method of analysis is similar to distinguishing individual personalities within the same human race. Such a precise procedure is not surprising in a large body like the human body, but the fact that it can be done in such microorganisms shows the progress of microbiology today). The length of gonococcus is equal to 1.6 μm (one micrometer is equal to one thousandth of a millimeter), and the width is even less than 1 μm (0.6 μm), so one can imagine its actual size. (Human blood, as seen with the naked eye, is a fluid, but we know that it is not)

It is something like water, containing a very large number of shaped bodies such as red blood cells and white blood cells. White blood cells are large, and red blood cells are small. These red blood cells are 7 μm in size. If we compare gonococcus to them, it is only a fraction of its volume.) Human white blood cells are two to three times larger than red blood cells (approximately 15 μm in length), and can contain more than a hundred gonococci (normally not so many). Gonococcus is a non-motile, heat-sensitive (damaged above 40 degrees Celsius), and desiccation-sensitive pathogen that is easily disinfected. Because its viability (outside the human body) is extremely small (usually only one hour), when culturing this pathogen, it is best to immediately inoculate it on a suitable (warm) culture medium after extracting the pathological fluid, so that better results can be obtained.

When it comes to examining gonococci, it is of course not difficult in acute gonorrhea (urethritis or conjunctivitis), but it is a more difficult problem in chronic gonorrhea. In addition to clinical symptom diagnosis and provocation, other bacteriological tests, such as serum reactions, microscopic examination of pus, and culture, are needed. If these methods are used at the right time, a large proportion of patients can be given a satisfactory diagnosis in today's situation. (The reason why I say this last sentence is because I have seen many patients who, after contracting this disease, feel great mental pain and are constantly in doubt, wondering if their gonorrhea is cured or not. Therefore, the speaker takes this opportunity to hope that those who are not yet infected will pay attention to prevention, and declares the great harm of venereal diseases.)

The amount of gonorrhea is directly proportional to the progress of civilization. Therefore, there are many people living in this 20th century who suffer from this disease. According to the statistics of German physician Erb, 50% of all his patients (2,000 men) had contracted this disease. According to the statistics of W Fisther, on average, people living in large cities (up to the age of 50) have been infected with gonorrhea one and a half times. Regardless of whether the above statistics are correct or not, the number of people suffering from this disease in the West is indeed not small. As our country gradually becomes Westernized, and Shanghai is one of the world's major cities, the number of people suffering from gonorrhea, although difficult to count, is undoubtedly not small.

Therefore, we must pay more attention to public health regarding this disease and other venereal diseases. The methods can be divided into two parts: First, the government can use special regulations to specifically manage venereal diseases that endanger the nation (Germany has a precedent). Second, popular propaganda (voluntary by the public) can be used to make the public understand the dangers of venereal diseases and their prevention methods.

Two major dangers of gonorrhea:

(1) Mothers with gonorrhea often infect their babies with the disease, resulting in ophthalmia neonatorum.

(2) Gonorrhea can reduce the national productivity (according to the statistics of Fischel, approximately 40% to 50% of infertile mothers are infertile because they have gonorrhea (other dangers to the body are temporarily not taken into account)).

Drug prevention:

Because gonococcus is extremely sensitive to silver preparations, Credé used it to drip into the eyes of newborns to prevent ophthalmia neonatorum. Later, some people applied this method to the genital area and also obtained considerable results (other chemicals are temporarily not taken into account).

In our country, we still have old-fashioned moral considerations. Many people are unwilling to treat this disease properly for fear that people will find out, especially women. In my opinion, this kind of thinking seems unnecessary, especially since doctors originally have an obligation to keep patients' secrets.

A Brief Discussion of Feverish Diseases (Part 1) 242

— Shen Kangbai

A healthy human body temperature is usually close to 37 degrees Celsius on a thermometer. Anything above this is considered a fever, which is commonly known as "cold and hot." The occurrence of fever is due to various pathogens invading the human body, causing an imbalance between the body's heat generation and dissipation regulation mechanisms, resulting in an increase in temperature and disturbances in the respiratory, digestive, circulatory, nervous, and excretory organs, which are commonly seen.

When chemical toxins or bacterial toxins invade the blood, causing fever through poisoning, it is called toxic fever. However, there are times when fever occurs without the invasion of fever-causing substances in the blood, which is called non-toxic fever, such as nervous fever caused by nerve disorders, or the strange fever patterns of hysteria.

The principle of body temperature increase is due to increased heat generation and decreased heat dissipation. The decrease in heat dissipation is due to the contraction of small arteries, resulting in reduced heat dissipation from the lungs and skin surface. At the same time, metabolic functions are abnormally enhanced, but the excess heat still cannot be reduced as a result.

The course of feverish diseases can be broadly divided into the following four stages:

(1) Increasing Stage: Feverish diseases vary in length and duration. When the body temperature begins to rise, the nerves around the blood vessels are stimulated, causing the capillaries of the skin to contract. At the same time, the pulse is fine, hard, and rapid, breathing is shallow, clear, and frequent, and there are uncomfortable sensations such as headache and chills. As heat generation increases and heat dissipation decreases, the body temperature rises rapidly to the second stage in about one or two hours. For those with prolonged fever, there is often no aversion to cold at the beginning, and the fever rises gradually, reaching the second stage after about one to several days.

(2) Peak Stage: This is the most severe stage of feverish diseases. The excitement of blood vessels and nerves remains unabated, and the increase in heat generation continues. Breathing is rapid, the pulse is frequent, and the patient experiences thirst, anxiety, fatigue, insomnia, loss of appetite, and reduced secretions. Moreover, due to the abnormality of muscle temperature and heat dissipation, the skin may be pale and cold, or flushed and hot. If the fever is too high, it can damage the heart muscle, resulting in heart failure. If the fever does not exceed 39 degrees Celsius, it may not cause any harm. The duration of this stage varies, from several hours to as long as several weeks, as in typhoid fever.

(3) Decreasing Stage: Once the patient reaches this stage, the skin's blood vessels gradually dilate and become congested. Profuse sweating increases heat dissipation, and the fever subsides. However, the length of the process varies. If the heat subsides in a short time, from two to three hours to thirty-six hours, it is called defervescence by crisis. If it takes a long time, from two to three days to three or four days, gradually decreasing by one or two degrees each morning until reaching normal temperature, it is called defervescence by lysis. After the fever subsides, although the pulse is still weak, the patient feels refreshed and relieved of a heavy burden, and falls asleep peacefully due to fatigue and thirst.

(4) Recovery Stage: Once the patient reaches this stage, the body temperature is often no different from when they were healthy. However, there are also cases where it drops below normal temperature, taking two or three days to return to normal. There are also those who experience mild fever every night during this stage.

The body temperature of feverish diseases usually decreases in the morning and rises in the evening. However, there are also cases where it rises in the morning and decreases in the evening, or fluctuates several times a day. Here, in the peak stage, I distinguish between the following three types based on the morning and evening fluctuations:

(1) Continued Fever (Febris Continea): The difference between morning and evening temperature fluctuations is minimal. The fever generally remains at the same level, often persisting for five or six days, or one or two weeks, before the fever subsides. It is seen in acute infectious diseases and acute inflammation.

(2) Remittent Fever (Febris Remitens): The difference between morning and evening fluctuations is very large, exceeding the norm. It is often seen in mild inflammation and chronic diseases.

(3) Intermittent Fever (Febris Intermittens): Normal temperature and high temperature alternate regularly, either every day, every other day, every three days, or every week. Examples include malaria and relapsing fever.

There are also ephemeral fever and atypical fever. The former lasts for a very short time, while the latter is an irregular fever with no fixed daily fluctuations. (To be continued)

The Current Society's Need for Medical Knowledge 243

— Wang Wanbai

The complexity and contradictions of medical concepts in our society have reached their peak today. When faced with a difficult-to-treat illness, people often resort to both Western and Chinese medicine haphazardly, without knowing what to do. They may be swayed by recommendations from relatives and friends or misled by exaggerated advertisements, trying them out without sufficient knowledge to distinguish and make decisions. This is one aspect.

Even when a doctor has been consulted, there is rarely long-term trust. People often judge the effectiveness of the treatment solely based on whether one dose of medicine shows immediate results. If not, they change doctors frequently without thinking it strange, and the doctors invited to treat lack the opportunity to be genuinely responsible. This is another aspect.

Patients are often very familiar with the prescriptions and medications of traditional Chinese doctors, frequently liking to participate in the discussion to show their knowledge. However, they lack basic scientific knowledge regarding the terminology and theories of modern medicine, often staring blankly and unable to understand. Therefore, trust cannot arise. This is a third aspect. Considering these points, if we want patients to benefit more from scientific treatments, we must disseminate common-sense knowledge of modern medicine to society on a large scale.

The most common methods used in the past to disseminate medical knowledge are twofold: one is literary propaganda, and the other is lectures at gatherings. These include medical articles in newspapers and magazines and health talks at meetings and schools. However, their effectiveness is limited to middle- and upper-class people who can read newspapers or a small number of occasional audience members. It is very difficult to find effective methods to enlighten the women in families who have the greatest authority over medical issues.

Recently, radio broadcasting has become popular because it can reach families in various locations, and people of all ages enjoy listening. Its influence is unparalleled. According to surveys, over 200,000 radios have already been sold in Shanghai. If proper methods are used for promotion, it would be an unparalleled tool for disseminating new medical knowledge.

Last spring, due to the war, I came to Shanghai and happened to witness the completion of the Chinese-Western Radio Station. The owner was an old friend and invited me to give talks on common medical knowledge at the station. I felt that this aligned with my long-held aspiration to serve society, so I agreed to fulfill this obligation, but I absolutely would not promote any individual or organization. Later, I gave systematic talks on new medical knowledge every day at noon. Unexpectedly, listeners from near and far sent letters expressing their appreciation, sometimes discussing medical issues. In my answers, I never recommended specific drugs, hospitals, or doctors, so listeners knew that what I said had no ulterior motive or background. Many listeners in various locations gathered friends and relatives at scheduled times to listen and recorded the lectures daily for study. The eagerness of society for medical knowledge is evident.

This winter, Christians, recognizing that commercial radio stations have too many entertainment programs and advertisements, initiated the establishment of a completely charitable gospel broadcasting station and appointed me to oversee everything. I specifically scheduled a medical and health program at 8 PM, the most convenient time, and invited people from the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau and the Physicians' Association to give talks on a rotating basis. Listeners from various locations responded with even greater enthusiasm. Now, other radio stations are also following suit, increasing their medical programming, which is a good phenomenon.

Based on past experience, radio broadcasting will inevitably become increasingly developed. New radio stations are also being built in various provinces and cities one after another. My colleagues in the new medical community should make good use of this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity to cooperate with radio stations in various locations and sacrifice their valuable time to undertake voluntary lectures to promote scientific understanding of new medicine to the public. If we can gather like-minded people and build our own radio station dedicated to medical and health education, the effect would be even greater. Are you all considering this?

Free Talk

Sister Flowers 244

— Meng Zhen

Ever since I watched the "Love and Hatred" starring Hu Die two years ago and regretted it immensely, I have been unwilling to watch domestic films no matter what. However, due to the promotion of friends, I recently watched "Sister Flowers" starring Hu Die. In this film, I must say that Hu Die has achieved success.

The events in this film, such as the warlords' exorbitant taxes and levies, extravagance, and debauchery, and the people's suffering, destitution, and displacement, although said to be from the 13th year of the Republic of China, are actually eternally new situations. Hu Die and the actress who played the old mother were able to realistically portray the plight of the poor, evoking shared emotions in the audience, which is precisely the success of art.

However, the problem raised by this film is not solved by its artistic success. From a purely artistic point of view, it is enough to present the facts, and it seems unnecessary to propose any solutions, as used in the Shanghai propaganda. This can be said to be a realistic approach. Its power lies in exposing the facts, reminding the world, and giving the audience a profound hint. But this is like the 19th century. Just as Ibsen's plays were called "problem plays," "Sister Flowers" only raises a problem. What other paths in life do ordinary people have besides sending their daughters to warlords as concubines or serving warlords?

After watching the film, on the way home from the New Light Cinema, I thought about this. Hu Die's cries seemed to still echo in my ears, and the painful scene of abandoning children and leaving home also seemed to flash before my eyes. I thought and walked across the road. Looking up, I saw the shop selling aviation lottery tickets facing me. Then the previous thought surfaced in my mind, "Isn't this a path in life?" Perhaps this is where the answer to the question raised by "Sister Flowers" lies. Unfortunately, this lottery only happens every few months. How wonderful it would be if there were a grand prize to be hoped for every day!

A Small Island in the South 245

— Yue Meng

During the day, climbing up the small slope, the surrounding green sea can be seen refreshing. At night, sleeping on the veranda, the myriad lights of Penang will rush towards you from the distant sea. This is a small island in the Indian Ocean, adjacent to the Malay Peninsula.

In mid-April 1930, I traveled from Burma to Singapore due to business. The ship passed Penang, intending to change course and land to take the Malay Federation train. Unexpectedly, the local health bureau detained me and a group of Indians on this small island to disinfect us for a week. The reason was that the places we departed from, such as Bombay, Madras, Calcutta, and Rangoon, had all been declared plague ports during the summer. (In India and Burma, schools start their summer vacations at the end of March in the Gregorian calendar.) However, this was limited to those of us traveling in third class because when we were invited onto the small boat to paddle to the small island, the first- and second-class passengers still joyfully and freely went ashore.

However, during this week, I truly enjoyed unprecedented tranquility. Every day, when the radiance of the red sun brushed away the morning mist on the sea, someone would run over to call us up, and the entire team would stand on the sand covered by the shade of trees, baring our upper bodies. The white doctor, leading three or four Malay assistants, would examine us one by one, as if an officer were inspecting new recruits, without any kindness. However, people who have always been disregarded by society can actually receive such care, which is truly gratifying. Although, there are other factors deeply hidden within. At about nine o'clock in the morning, a ration was usually given to each person, such as dried fish, potatoes, milk, and eggs, which were always sufficient. As for the Indians, perhaps because they were Indians, they could especially receive beef or chicken.

We lived in military-style (Camp) houses, with walls that were empty above the waist. The clear sea breeze and the bright moon in the mountains could freely visit us. During the long days, we had nothing to do, so we climbed up on the walls and sat, leisurely watching the sails swaying on the waves, whistling softly. At night, we slept on the smooth cement floor, listening quietly to the songs of the South Indians, and drifted happily into dreams. Half of the open space outside the house was paved with cement, which could be used for walking in the morning and evening and for drying clothes. The other half was covered with mud and sand, shaded by green trees. Twice a day, we would light a bonfire under the trees to cook food.

Among the many Indians, besides me, a wanderer from a foreign land, there was also a family from Bhutan. The melancholy atmosphere of their small family often attracted my attention. The man was short and sturdy, with a long curved knife hanging on his waist. His head was shaved, leaving only a tuft of hair on the top, which looked like a child's. This was originally a religious symbol. Hindu followers in India generally had this style. It seems that Bhutanese culture is greatly influenced by India. He seemed to be constantly angry, and two ragged and dirty children sat blankly by their mother's side all day, seemingly too scared to move. The mother pursed her lips and quietly mended her torn clothes. When I saw them, I felt as if I were on the Himalayas, facing the gloomy sky and the snow that never melts. The bright light of the southern country seemed to be of no benefit to them! I wanted to ask, "Why did you leave your hometown?" But I didn't know what language to use because I didn't understand Bhutanese. However, a week of contact told me everything in their eyebrows. Can't a wanderer see the wandering factors of another person?

Random Notes (Continued) 246

— Xia Chang

(5)

Some people indignantly say that the social changes in China over the past decade or so are reflected in literary works as nothing more than a blank sheet of paper. This statement is certainly an overstatement, but it shows that creation cannot powerfully reflect society. Therefore, the production of great works is really not an easy thing. An Zhiyuan wrote to Cai Manfu, saying, "People often say that the An Lushan Rebellion only resulted in a collection of poems by Du Fu. Since the Bingzi year (1936), for more than a decade, such a huge world has been repeatedly manipulated and reorganized several times, resulting in today's situation. I wonder if there are still any old men like Du Fu who are observing from the sidelines? Having the time but not the talent is also a great flaw of heaven and earth." This is truly a portrait of today's literary scene. I am looking forward to the production of great works.

(6)

Xu Fang also said, "The Chu madman Jieni is the most of the Spring and Autumn period."

A cold person. However, savoring his words, he is not the coldest person in the world, but precisely the hottest person in the world. When it is extremely hot and there is nothing to be done, one has to return to the cold. Extreme heat inevitably leads to extreme cold, which is why one sighs while riding a raft." This is precisely the origin of the production of so-called humor literature and satire literature.

(7)

"Sorrow" and "illness" are the capital of scholars. This statement is very strange, but it is also the most common and most ordinary explanation throughout history. Zeng Furen wrote to Qiu Xiaolu, saying, "Your letter says that you are in sorrow and illness. These two words are the capital for us scholars to read and write books. If we were in happiness and strength, we would not know how much more romantic and enjoyable it would be, and it may not be harmful to static exercises." This is nothing more than adding a footnote to this statement.

(8)

According to Li Qing, rewriting is also one of the competitions among literati. He said, "People only know that dripping ink on paper and writing hundreds of words in a moment is the ultimate. But they do not know that wielding the pen and writing dozens of lines in a moment is also the ultimate joy. Knowing it yourself is like this, let alone the onlookers. In the past, Yuan Fuchu had a work, and Yu Bosheng reduced it by one hundred and twenty words, and Fuchu also shouted quickly and accurately. This is a competition among literati."

Miscellaneous Talk on Humor 247

— Xu Maoyong

The year 1933 was the "National Products Year" for the Chinese people, but for the "Shanghai School" literati, it was the "Humor Year." The most popular articles this year were humor articles. Compared to the "National Products Year" with "200 million yuan of imported Japanese goods," the achievements of the "Humor Year" seem to be much better. From "The Analects" onwards, many publications, large and small, were swept away by the trend of humor. And the remaining influence has not yet faded. Probably in this "Women's National Products Year" of 1934, the sales of "The Analects" will still not decrease, right?

What is "humor"? Everyone already knows that it is the translated name of a foreign word, Humor. What kind of thing is Humor? Many experts discussed it in "The Analects" last year, but they still couldn't give us a clue. Until recently, Mr. Lin Yutang's three articles on humor, upper, middle, and lower, can be said to be the most detailed theory on humor. Detailed is detailed, but still, he still cannot give us a concrete, clear, and simple definition. Probably, as Maurice Decobra said, the question of "what is humor" is "a more troublesome problem than the problem of universal gravitation! It is an irregular polygon in literary criticism! No one can ever analyze the psychology of a humor writer. This psychology is elusive, like a butterfly chased by biologists. Just when you think you have caught it, it escapes."

Speaking of Maurice Decobra, everyone remembers that he was a French writer who came to Shanghai last year. The Shanghainese welcomed him as a humorist, like welcoming Bernard Shaw, but of course not as grandly as welcoming Shaw. As usual, our journalists held an oral exam for him, and he answered with humorous remarks, but according to "The Analects," his answers did not count as humor. Moreover, his words that he found Chinese women very beautiful and was fascinated by them aroused the protest of a "girl" in Beiping, which was very boring. From this, we can also know that he is not a skilled humorist.

But he is putting his heart into studying humor. Recently, I saw a book he wrote called "Laughter in the Fog," which is an anthology of English and American humor writers he edited. In the front is his preface, entitled "Anglo-Saxon Humor."

The opening of this preface is the few sentences quoted above. Then, he said, "Many people often try to define humor. Some propose archaeological definitions, some propose philosophical ambiguous and profound definitions, some propose Euclidean theorem-like strict definitions... and various others. These all have some truth, but none of them are perfect."

Therefore, he spent another effort soliciting definitions of humor from many English and American humor writers.

Many people responded to his work. Now I will copy a few of them below:

"Humor cannot be defined. It is a major element that makes people laugh." — George Bernard Shaw

"I don't believe that humor can be explained. But in my opinion, humor is something that... moves us with its humor." — Jerome K. Jerome

"I often think that humor is like the oxygen in the air we breathe. It creates and maintains human laughter. It can certainly create many other more important things, but laughter is the first." — R. C. Carton

"Humor is the smile in the eyes of the wise." — Israel Zangwill

"Alas! I am always trying to define humor, but I always fail! The most popular attitude among us is: it is better to mock the protagonist of a story than to laugh with him." — W. Pett Ridge

"We might say that this is the pleasant thought of someone who is not worldly." — F. Anstey

People often distinguish wit and humor from the distinction of race or country. They say that wit is a characteristic of the Latin race, while humor belongs to the northern race, such as the Anglo-Saxons or Scandinavians. I think this distinction is arbitrary because there are many examples proving that Northerners also have wit, and Southern Europeans also have humor. I think the difference between the two is actually produced by different temperaments. In my opinion, humor is a subtle observation of the ever-changing life, and it is the satirical power that destroys melancholy thoughts. This satire sometimes takes a serious attitude and sometimes takes a playful attitude. In short, it is to make us temporarily feel the meaninglessness of those things that disturb our hearts." — W. L. Courteney (To be continued)

No Snow (3) 248

— Miao Chongqun

The station is very lively today: the train is crowded with all kinds of people, and the platform is also crowded with all kinds of people. In the dark mass, there are also coffins nailed with six planks, canvas beds with no one lying on them, bundles of large guns, and bundles of hand grenades made by Shanxi people... On the opposite train, red cross flags and swastika flags are inserted, and it is full of soldiers who are seriously injured and cannot move...

The closer to the locomotive, the more chaotic it is; in fact, the locomotive has not yet arrived, and even if it arrives, it will probably be drowned out by this chaotic noise and cannot be heard. But the further back you go, the quieter it becomes, and the degree of quietness can be followed by the number of vehicles: second class | second class | first class | first class dining car | first class sleeping car... Wagon-Lits sleeping car...

This time, the Wagon-Lits sleeping car contained an urn of ashes of an "international hero." Two wreaths were placed on one side, setting off this originally magnificent car even more beautifully and lively.

All the Japanese soldiers who had just come out of the protection zone were gathered here. They lined up along the train in two rows, like two "heaven cards" connected together.

An officer with a thick Charlie Chaplin-style mustache looked very hurried and serious, going up and down the car for a while. As the departure time was approaching, he ran to Shuiguan in the most regular pace. Because the sound of his running footsteps calmed our chaotic station a lot, and naturally opened a way for him. From this moment of calmness, we could see our traffic police, station master | wearing three layers and eight layers of golden hoops | quietly hiding in the crowd like ghosts. An officer in a formal dress and a thousand-layer-sole shoes even turned his head when he was lighting a cigarette. What was he thinking? On the front line, we will eventually have a day to meet!

The departure bell rang, and the officer with the Charlie Chaplin mustache hurried back. He held a three-legged bronze incense burner and a few incense sticks in his hand, running as regularly as when he left. It was just that his mustache was too heavy, fanning up and down as he ran, as if it were really fake, losing some dignity and carrying a funny taste.

"Wo Lou Wo Lou!"

Not understanding what he was shouting, the two rows of short-legged soldiers stood at attention following this command.

The car began to move.

Soon, there was another sound:

"Wo Lou Wo Lou! Wo Li Lou!"

This time the sound seemed a little more complicated, but it was even more unclear what it meant. Only saw that the two rows of short-legged soldiers changed from two rows of "heaven cards" to four rows of "long threes." They saluted the train that was gradually moving away. On our train were "warriors wrapped in horsehide corpses" | on our train were executioners who slaughtered our own parents, elders, and brothers.

The station suddenly became much quieter. Only those wounded soldiers who could not leave were left, lying there without even groaning. There were also the thin-slab coffins that were left behind, containing the bones of our silent and unnamed warriors.

The outside of the station was really lively to death. Tens of thousands of pieces of luggage were almost piled up in the middle of the street. Who knows where they are going to be transported?
