The Bitter Life of Literati 249

— Jun

The global economic panic is spreading everywhere like wildfire. The merchant class can be said to be the most affected, especially small-capital businesses. The fall in prices, the reduction in purchasing power, and the closure or bankruptcy of stores on the market that cannot be maintained are happening every day. Under this atmosphere of recession, the sharp decline in the bookstore business is naturally not surprising.

In a previous article in this publication, Mr. Wen Li wrote an article "New Books Sold by the Catty." After reading this news, what I felt was truly a mixture of crying and laughter.

In this day and age, except for a very few writers with special status, whose monthly income is enough to cover food, clothing, and shelter, almost all other pen-holders are living fragmented lives, gritting their teeth and dealing with the poor ghost all day long. Occasionally, there are clever and capable people who change their careers or rush into officialdom, but that is very rare. And those who have no other way to go can only bury themselves in hard work until they die of poverty and starvation.

Living by eating one's own blood is painful enough, but what is even more tragic is that even if one exhausts one's blood, one cannot obtain even the minimum warmth and food, and is still oppressed by hunger and cold. Famous writers can still use their reputation to gain various conveniences in their sales, but what about unknown writers? It is not known how many difficulties, many twists and turns, and the white eyes of the big-bellied merchants they go through before they can sell a manuscript and obtain even enough to compensate for the loss of paper and pens.

In the past, people often regarded literati as remarkable figures in society. That is a big mistake. In fact, the status and life of literati in society are not as good as everyone else. To say it sadly, they are far inferior to the prostitute class. Prostitutes only sell their bodies in exchange for considerable remuneration, while literati not only sell their bodies, but also sell their souls, and the result is not worth the loss. What is more sorrowful than this?

Originally, books that cannot be eaten when hungry or worn when cold should have long been regarded as insignificant toys by some people.

The fact that mental laborers are despised by the world is just what one expects. In fact, the suffering and sorrow bestowed upon literati by this volatile era is truly too much. Since one cannot survive by walking this path, should one give up and change careers? In this society with more people than opportunities, it is not easy to find a job, so one has to continue to make a living by selling one's blood and brains, while struggling and panting under the heavy pressure of poverty and sorrow. The cruelty and coldness of society towards literati is already terrifying enough, and now there is news of new books being sold by the catty. I wonder what the writers who make a living by writing think of this event that is worth crying about. The decline of the market is becoming more and more serious day by day. In the future, it is difficult to predict what kind of situation it will become. Perhaps even more tragic encounters will follow one after another. At that time, a group of people who live by writing will have to wait for death.

Home 250

— Dai Ni

Random Notes on Returning Home

Not the mother's son, but the grandmother's grandson.

After running to Shanghai on a forgotten day, and through the desperate efforts of two people, we tore through five sets of calendars amidst illness and poverty. Last year, my wife's pregnancy shattered the position of a primary school teacher earning twenty-eight dollars a month. Adding insult to injury, I suffered from a long illness. So, as the child was about to be born, I reluctantly wrote home, like a bell-ringing monk, to ask for some money. The reply was the expected disappointment. Nevertheless, the child was naturally born into this sinful world. A simple letter: "On such and such date, at such and such time, a boy was born, mother and child are safe," sent by registered mail. Unexpectedly, a return letter arrived, talking about the child and such, mostly suitable for childcare tips, and finally saying to bring him back to see her, the grandmother, after the first month. As usual, he should naturally be brought back so that I could add some glory to the child’s face. Although he might not be a true emperor in the future, the firstborn boy in the hometown is still considered a joyous occasion. However, for me, with wasted opportunities to earn money and additional expenses like travel costs, it would be a loss to just go back for a "look." So, I made excuses about "bodily discomfort" and used the blind man's trick of "not traveling" to get by.

At the end of the lunar year, an unexpected letter arrived again: "Come back with the child for the New Year's greetings, no matter what!" This was an order, with the serious implication of "disobedience will be punished severely." So, I had no choice but to hold the child and "go down to Jiangnan."

Stepping onto the soil of my hometown from the train station, it seemed like I was familiar with everyone, yet they were all strangers. Rickshaws pulled along the road, and I saw many "small feet enlarged feet" style modern foreign houses. My hometown seemed no longer mine. "Ah! Five years!" I sighed softly, walking home as if in a dream.

Five old trees stood tall in front of the door. They recognized me. A gust of wind passed, and they called out in unison, "Home!" Yes, "Home!" I looked up at the dilapidated old house, half-supported by two thick wooden props, its fate probably sealed. "Home! Home, separated for five years!"

The rickshaw stopped at the door. An elderly woman looked at us as if we were foreigners. I recognized her; she was the old servant of my grandmother, so loyal, just like the old servants in old novels. But she could only guard the dilapidated house and couldn't perform a story of saving the young master. I called her name, and she squinted her eyes and ran out the door. "Really, the young master and mistress are back, hahaha, young master!" She forgot her age and snatched the child from my wife's arms. Holding him in her arms, she said, "Oh, how heavy! Wu Ma is useless!" The next sentence was almost to herself. However, she sighed and happily ran inside to announce the news.

My mother stood in the main room, smiling as she held her grandson. Wu Ma bustled about as if many guests had arrived at the house, busying herself with this and that. Although she couldn't save the young master, she was indeed loyal to him. Poor old woman!

Before "bring the child back" in the letter, it was "New Year's greetings," which was also a major event. I seemed to have forgotten that a son had a set of rituals for his mother. My wife reminded me so as not to fail in my duty.

The child cried. My wife took him from my mother's arms. The mother-in-law and daughter-in-law stood together, and I found my wife surprisingly old. It is said that women age easily after giving birth. My mother had two sons, although the current son was not hers. In terms of age and childbirth, my mother shouldn't be so young compared to my wife. My wife's aging seemed mythical. A twenty-two-year-old young woman!

My eyelids heavy with shame, I ran to the hall to look at my father's portrait. He was also young. My hand naturally reached down to my chin, and the prickly stubble told me that I had exceeded my father's age. At this moment, I lost consciousness, not knowing how long I stayed there, until my mother woke me up. She asked what I was doing in the hall. I casually replied, "Looking at the flowers I planted."

"They all died long ago," she said, her voice raised particularly high.

"Fool!" I scolded myself. Five years! A few small flowers and plants, subjected to natural destruction and without human protection, how could they not die? Just like people, a twenty-four-year-old youth!

I hysterically ran outside alone.

Returning for dinner under the kerosene lamp, my wife and I sat facing each other. My mother held her grandson, standing at the head of the table. Suddenly, the child cried, and my mother, talking about the child and such, tried to coax him with childcare tips. But the true emperor was extraordinary; he waved his little fists and kept crying.

"Recognizing his mother?" The experienced mother didn't trust that her methods would completely fail.

My wife put down her rice bowl and took the child. He waved his little fists and smiled.

"Recognizing his mother?" I said.

My wife smiled, so content, something I hadn't seen since we got married.

There was no sound at the head of the table. I lowered my head to eat, pushing each grain of rice into my mouth.

Modern Celebrity Calligraphy and Painting 251

— Calligraphy by Mr. Wu Renye

Quietly Reading Your Excellency's Articles, Drum and Clepsydra Sound, Sitting Alone at Dusk, Who Are You? Strategizing, Beautiful

Fear of Death and Suicide 252

— Jue

Opening the newspaper, news of suicides meets the eye every day. Every time I see this kind of news, I always feel that this is an act that should not be done. At the same time, there are some people who vigorously praise the courage of those who commit suicide and ridicule my attitude as being afraid of death. I myself dare not admit that I have the courage to commit suicide, but to say that I am afraid of death, I absolutely cannot admit. The general view is that suicide and fear of death are two relative terms. Those who commit suicide are not afraid of death, and those who fear death will not commit suicide. There is absolutely no contradiction in my thinking like this. In fact, both death and life have their true meanings. I would like to use a corner of this column to propose a discussion in order to explore what our attitude should be.

We must know that we do not meet death. When death comes, the person no longer exists. When the person exists, there is no death. We cannot find the word "death" in our dictionary, because when we die, our dictionary will also be destroyed along with us. Therefore, the saying "fear of death," when boiled down, really carries a bit of a ridiculous meaning! I have heard a story: A fortune teller made a bet with someone, saying that the world would be completely destroyed in ten years. That person did not believe it, saying that it would absolutely not happen. The two sides could not agree, so they bet a thousand dollars. Later, someone asked him, where did you get so much money to bet with people? What if you lose? The person smiled and said, if the world is really destroyed, there will be neither him nor me, so how can there be a loss! Although this is a joke, carefully considering its meaning can make us understand what the relationship between man and flowers really is. Therefore, the meaning of the word "death" is only the moment when we humans leave this world. Its relationship with life is sudden. When death comes, a person's senses are immediately cut off. We ourselves can never experience what death is like. So, if a person cannot experience death, then what is there to be afraid of! At the same time, the process of life may be full of reefs, which often makes us feel difficulties in moving forward. Because we are unwilling to fight with difficulties, we then resort to self-destruction in order to escape this society, out of sight, out of mind. But this is only a temporary emotional distortion. In fact, since we were born into this world and nurtured by our parents and society, having grown into a person, we have no choice but to be a person and should never abandon their responsibilities, which is a sin. As for saying that environmental difficulties cannot be resolved, I dare not agree. The reason is not that the difficulties cannot be resolved, but that he himself is unwilling to continue to fight with the difficulties. Suicide is fundamentally an act of the weak, which, except for those who worship death, cannot arouse people's sympathy. Its errors do not need to be discussed in many pages, and the matter is clearly placed before us.

In short, fear of death is certainly not good, and the history of suicide should not be. We only have to grasp reality, because the past is counted. We absolutely do not know the future, only reality can we grasp. Strutting forward, this is what a good man should do.

Illegally Felled Ancient Cypress Trees 253

— Qiqi

Reported in the news: "Beiping (Beijing) Telegram: The Ancient Relics Preservation Committee discovered illegal felling of cypress trees. In addition to the Temple of Heaven and the Altar of Agriculture, there are also a total of one hundred and three trees in the Altar of the Sun and the Altar of the Earth that are either insect-infested or withered. Also, there are many trees in the Imperial Academy that have been marked for felling, and the prices quoted by the Tan Ji Quan Lumber Factory are different. The committee has telegraphed the Ministry of Interior for thorough investigation. Public opinion is paying more attention to this matter. A newspaper commented that the Ministry of Interior should bear full responsibility, because the felling was done by people sent by the Ministry of Interior. If the trees have insects, they can be exterminated, there is no reason to destroy them completely." After reading this piece of news, we feel that it is indeed news.

Since the "September 18th Incident," the ancient relics of Beiping were moved south. The meaning is that ancient relics are precious treasures and cannot be lost along with the possible loss of Beiping. Therefore, they were moved south to be preserved in the Shanghai Concession, which is very fortunate (although it is known that some were lost on the long journey south from Beiping by boat (?), but most of them are safe and complete). Now that Beiping is under the watchful eyes of a strong neighbor, no one dares to predict what will happen in the future. In addition to ancient relics and antiques, ancient cypress trees in Beiping are also valuable. If the cypress trees are not moved south, there should be a proper way to deal with them. The Ministry of Interior sent people to cut down the ancient cypress trees. Although the intention has not been announced, it is obviously for the sake of preserving the national culture that the cypress trees are cut down and moved south. The public opinion in Beiping is truly short-sighted and has no foresight. Can't they even think of this reason? And a certain newspaper is even more strange, clearly recording that it was the Ministry of Interior that sent people to cut down the trees, but it is titled "Illegally Felled," and the article also says "because the felling was done by people sent by the Ministry of Interior," etc. This is simply lawless! The "illegal fellers" are criminals, how can they be directly called "sent by the Ministry of Interior?" If you want to say that they were sent by the Ministry of Interior, you should at least say that the fellers cannot be labeled as criminals. Chinese people are most likely to make a fuss over trifles, especially most likely to shout loudly over small matters. The illegal felling of ancient cypress trees is thousands of miles away from the loss of national territory. What's so great about the illegal felling of ancient cypress trees, especially when the illegal fellers were sent by the government? Moreover, the meaning of the illegal felling of ancient cypress trees is clearly the same as that of ancient relics, to be moved south to ensure their eternal preservation?

Price Increase 254

— Nier

Getting off the No. 5 tram every day and buying a Da Wan Evening News from a woman has become a habit. A friend asked me why I don't subscribe to one and have it delivered to my little apartment. I shook my head; in fact, I had no reason to answer.

Today, I took the newspaper from the old woman's hand. She exceptionally asked for six copper coins instead of the usual four. I asked her if the price had increased. She smiled and said, "Today is the lottery drawing."

So, the price increase is due to the lottery drawing. These two things linked together are indeed a "problem."

I regret not accepting my friend's advice. On the day of each aviation lottery drawing, I will lose two more copper coins. If it returns to the period when lotteries were prevalent, no matter how lazy I am, I will definitely take a rickshaw to the newspaper office to subscribe to one. The rickshaw fare can probably be produced anyway.

Lulu's Victory (2) 255

— Written by Italian M. Sellao, Translated by Jing Xin

"Gu Gang won!" I shouted. "No," Meng Tefulan smiled and said, "Laweilou won." I was angry that he opposed me like this, but he continued to smile and oppose me; as a result, we made a bet. Finally, after half an hour of heartbeat and unease, I realized that Gu Gang had lied to me, I lost, and Meng Tefulan won, think about it! I told him that I would pay him immediately; he bowed to me and said not to be in such a hurry. Afterwards, I met him in Qi Ya Jia and gave him a questioning look. He smiled mysteriously and bowed to me. Meeting in the theater was the same, and it was the same no matter where I met him. I became very curious. Robert is handsome and twenty-six years old. So, this morning, Robert's father, my future father-in-law, and mother discussed for two hours.

"Ah!"

"Is this a sign that you are listening carefully to me?" Oh, I know he has visited Yang Nait. Marriage is arranged like this. One major thing has not yet been decided: when should I go to the town hall, should I wear a gray dress, or a brown dress? Should I wear a hat with ribbons or no ribbons?"

"How far are you going to go with this madness!"

"Madness? Of course, there is no obstacle at all. Robert and I will love each other madly, and our parents are also satisfied — —"

"Are you willing to marry someone like this?"

"What do you mean by "like this"? The meaning of this sentence is too vague."

"Marry him without understanding him or loving him?"

"But I really understand him. I have seen him on the racetrack and on the road. I adore him! I didn't have a snack the day before yesterday because I didn't see him, and I didn't even drink three cups of coffee. I really wanted to commit suicide." "But what about him?"

"He is willing to marry me, so he loves me!" Lulu answered triumphantly. But when she saw the paleness on Sophia's face, she regretted that she shouldn't have said that, so she leaned towards her sister and asked affectionately:

"Did I say something that offended you?"

"No, dear, no; you are right. A person loves, and a person marries. It is difficult to awaken love," so she sighed softly.

"Awakening love, awakening love!" Lulu said repeatedly in a frantic manner. "It's easy, Sophia; but if a person has such a solemn look like you, melancholy eyes, and a face that doesn't smile, if a person walks and thinks, and sits in the corner and thinks, while others are dancing and making noise, if a person only reads and doesn't laugh, he is not living but falling in love, but naturally he has developed a good
